The Mu'tazilite Proof from Quran 16:90 and Its Refutation
Sanusi refutes the Mu'tazilite scriptural proof from Quran 16:90.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Ash'aris refute the Mu'tazilite claim that Quran 16:90 proves actions are intrinsically good or evil before divine command.

Core Idea
The words 'commands' and 'prohibits' establish the ruling, not prior intrinsic values.

The Mu'tazilites often cite Quran 16:90 to argue that justice and goodness are known rationally before revelation. Sanusi here dissects their proof and shows that the verse actually supports the Ash'ari position: moral qualities are determined by the command, not prior to it. Let's examine this crucial refutation.

Guided Path
1
Read the Mu'tazilite proof
Read the passage describing how the Mu'tazilites interpret Quran 16:90 to claim that justice and goodness are established before the command.
Notice they think the verse implies an prior moral order.
2
Identify the Ash'ari counter-argument
Sanusi explains that the verbs 'commands' and 'prohibits' indicate that the ruling itself is established by the command—the qualities are not intrinsic but become good or evil by the command.
He also distinguishes this from customary good/evil.
3
Understand the distinction from customary good/evil
Sanusi clarifies that the verse is not about al-tahsin wa'l-taqbih al-'urfiyyan (customary good/evil), which is based on social norms, not rational necessity.
4
Reflect on why this matters
Ask yourself: If good and evil are not intrinsic, what does that imply about God's commands? This is a key point in Ash'ari theology.
It preserves God's absolute sovereignty.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وشبهة المعتزلة النصية في الحُسْن والقبح العقليين : نحو قوله سبحانه وتعالى عن سوء فهمهم : هو إِنَّ اللَّهَ يَأْمُرُ بِالْعَدْلِ وَالْإِحْسَنِ فأثبتهما بزعمهم قبل الأمر ، وَيَنْهَى عَنِ الْفَحْشَاءِ وَالْمُنكَرِ وَالْبَغْيِ ﴾ [النحل : ٩٠] فأثبتهما بزعمهم قبل النهي ونحو حديث سيدنا معاذ رضي الله عنه الذي رواه مسلم ( ١٠٠٦ ) : أيأتي أحدنا شهوته ويكون له فيها أجر ؟! قال صلى الله عليه وسلم : « أرأيتُم لو وضعَها في حرام أكانَ عليهِ فيها وزرٌ ؟ فكذلك إذا وضعها في الحلالِ كَانَ لهُ أجر . وإنما الآية حُجَّةٌ عليهم ؛ إذ كلمتا ( يأمر ) و( ينهى ) دلتا على تأسيس الحكم ، وكأنَّ العدل والإحسان والفحشاء والمنكر والبغي في رتبة واحدة قبل الأمر والنهي ، ثم تفرّقتا بهما ، وهذا غير التحسين والتقبيح العرفيين ، وأما الحديث فهو من باب قياس العكس (۱) قال الإمام الرازي في الأربعين ) ( ١ / ٣٥٠ ) : ( اتفقت المعتزلة على أنَّ أفعال الله تعالى وأحكامه معللة برعاية مصالح العباد ، وهو اختيار أكثر المتأخرين من الفقهاء ، وهذا عندنا باطل )
And the scriptural proof (shubha) of the Mu'tazilites concerning rational good and evil (al-husn wa'l-qubh al-'aqliyyayn): such as His saying, Exalted and Majestic, in misinterpretation of their understanding: He [said?] 'Indeed, Allah commands justice and goodness' — so they claim that they [justice and goodness] are established before the command; 'and prohibits immorality, evil, and transgression' [Quran 16:90] — so they claim that they [immorality, evil, and transgression] are established before the prohibition. And similar to it is the hadith of our master Mu'adh, may Allah be pleased with him, which Muslim narrated (1006): 'Does any one of us come to his desire and have reward in it?' The Prophet, peace be upon him, said: 'Do you see that if he placed it in the unlawful, would he have sin in it? So likewise, if he places it in the lawful, he has reward.' But indeed the verse is a proof against them, since the two words 'commands' and 'prohibits' indicate the establishment of the ruling, and as if justice, goodness, immorality, evil, and transgression are in one rank before the command and prohibition, and then they become differentiated by them. And this is other than customary good and evil (al-tahsin wa'l-taqbih al-'urfiyyan). As for the hadith, it is from the chapter of qiyas al-'aks (inverse analogy). Imam al-Razi said in al-Arba'in (1/350): 'The Mu'tazilites have agreed that the actions of Allah and His rulings are caused by considerations of the interests of the servants, and this is the choice of most of the later jurists, and this is false in our view.'
Source pages p. 294

Commentary
This passage presents the Mu'tazilite scriptural proof for rational good and evil (al-husn wa'l-qubh al-'aqliyyayn) and then refutes it from an Ash'ari perspective. The author describes the Mu'tazilite argument: they cite Quran 16:90, where Allah commands justice and goodness and prohibits immorality, evil, and transgression. The Mu'tazilites claim that these qualities (justice, goodness, etc.) must be intrinsically good or evil before the command or prohibition, because the command presumes the goodness of the commanded, and the prohibition presumes the evil of the prohibited. They also cite the hadith of Mu'adh where the Prophet indicates that lawful sexual relations can have reward, implying that the act itself has a moral quality before the ruling. The Ash'ari refutation is twofold. First, regarding the verse: the words 'commands' and 'prohibits' actually show that the ruling is established by the command/prohibition; the qualities are on the same level before the command, and differentiation occurs only by the command. This means that the good and evil are not intrinsic but determined by the Sharia. The author notes that this is different from customary good and evil (al-'urfiyyan), which are based on social norms, not rational necessity. Second, the hadith is explained as an example of qiyas al-'aks (inverse analogy): if an act in the unlawful has sin, then the same act in the lawful has reward — but this does not prove intrinsic moral value; it is a legal analogy, not a rational proof. The passage ends with a quote from Imam al-Razi confirming that the Mu'tazilite position that God's actions and rulings are motivated by considerations of the interests of creatures is false according to the Ash'aris.

Key Terms
شبهة المعتزلة
الحُسْن والقبح العقليين
الأمر والنهي
التحسين والتقبيح العرفيين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Quran 16:90 proves that actions are intrinsically good or evil before divine command.
Correction: The verse actually shows that the command itself establishes the moral quality; the actions are not intrinsically good or evil prior to the command.

Checkpoint
According to the Ash'ari refutation in this passage, what do the words 'commands' and 'prohibits' in Quran 16:90 indicate?
A) That justice and goodness exist intrinsically before the command.
B) That the ruling is established by the command and prohibition, not that the qualities are intrinsic.
C) That God is obliged to command good and forbid evil.
D) That the Mu'tazilites are correct.

Key Takeaway
The Ash'aris argue that Quran 16:90 does not prove intrinsic moral values; rather, it shows that commands themselves establish moral rulings.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read Quran 16:90, do you instinctively assume that justice is good because you feel it is, or because Allah declares it so? What does this lesson reveal about the source of your moral convictions? Commit to consciously affirming Allah's authority over every moral judgment today.
?
Is there any command of Allah that you find difficult to accept as good because it conflicts with your own sense of right and wrong? How does this lesson challenge you to submit your inner moral compass to divine command? Will you pray for humility to accept His rulings without reservation?
?
This lesson refutes the idea that actions have value independent of Allah's command. In what area of your life do you still act as if your own standards define good and evil? What would it take for you to let go of that attitude and fully embrace divine sovereignty over moral values?

The Hadith of Mu'adh and the Ash'ari Rebuttal
Sanusi refutes the Mu'tazilite proof from the hadith of Mu'adh and quotes al-Razi.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Ash'aris refute the Mu'tazilite proof from the hadith of Mu'adh and the broader principle that God's actions are not motivated by created interests.

Core Idea
The hadith is an inverse analogy, not a proof of intrinsic moral value.

The Mu'tazilites also cite a hadith where the Prophet states that lawful sexual relations can have reward, implying an intrinsic moral quality. Sanusi explains that this is an example of qiyas al-'aks (inverse analogy) and therefore does not prove rational good/evil. He then seals the refutation with a quote from al-Razi rejecting the Mu'tazilite position that God's actions are caused by created interests.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith and the Mu'tazilite use
Read the hadith of Mu'adh and understand why the Mu'tazilites think it supports rational good/evil.
They argue that reward for a lawful act implies it is intrinsically good.
2
Understand qiyas al-'aks
Sanusi calls this 'inverse analogy'. Learn what that means and why it does not prove intrinsic value.
It is a legal reasoning tool, not a metaphysical proof.
3
Consider the Razi quote
Al-Razi affirms that the Mu'tazilite view that God's actions are motivated by created interests is false according to the Ash'aris.
This reinforces the Ash'ari position that morality is command-based.
4
Reflect on the overall argument
Combine both proofs: the verse and the hadith. How does the Ash'ari refutation uphold the sovereignty of God's command?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وشبهة المعتزلة النصية في الحُسْن والقبح العقليين : نحو قوله سبحانه وتعالى عن سوء فهمهم : هو إِنَّ اللَّهَ يَأْمُرُ بِالْعَدْلِ وَالْإِحْسَنِ فأثبتهما بزعمهم قبل الأمر ، وَيَنْهَى عَنِ الْفَحْشَاءِ وَالْمُنكَرِ وَالْبَغْيِ ﴾ [النحل : ٩٠] فأثبتهما بزعمهم قبل النهي ونحو حديث سيدنا معاذ رضي الله عنه الذي رواه مسلم ( ١٠٠٦ ) : أيأتي أحدنا شهوته ويكون له فيها أجر ؟! قال صلى الله عليه وسلم : « أرأيتُم لو وضعَها في حرام أكانَ عليهِ فيها وزرٌ ؟ فكذلك إذا وضعها في الحلالِ كَانَ لهُ أجر . وإنما الآية حُجَّةٌ عليهم ؛ إذ كلمتا ( يأمر ) و( ينهى ) دلتا على تأسيس الحكم ، وكأنَّ العدل والإحسان والفحشاء والمنكر والبغي في رتبة واحدة قبل الأمر والنهي ، ثم تفرّقتا بهما ، وهذا غير التحسين والتقبيح العرفيين ، وأما الحديث فهو من باب قياس العكس (۱) قال الإمام الرازي في الأربعين ) ( ١ / ٣٥٠ ) : ( اتفقت المعتزلة على أنَّ أفعال الله تعالى وأحكامه معللة برعاية مصالح العباد ، وهو اختيار أكثر المتأخرين من الفقهاء ، وهذا عندنا باطل )
And the scriptural proof (shubha) of the Mu'tazilites concerning rational good and evil (al-husn wa'l-qubh al-'aqliyyayn): such as His saying, Exalted and Majestic, in misinterpretation of their understanding: He [said?] 'Indeed, Allah commands justice and goodness' — so they claim that they [justice and goodness] are established before the command; 'and prohibits immorality, evil, and transgression' [Quran 16:90] — so they claim that they [immorality, evil, and transgression] are established before the prohibition. And similar to it is the hadith of our master Mu'adh, may Allah be pleased with him, which Muslim narrated (1006): 'Does any one of us come to his desire and have reward in it?' The Prophet, peace be upon him, said: 'Do you see that if he placed it in the unlawful, would he have sin in it? So likewise, if he places it in the lawful, he has reward.' But indeed the verse is a proof against them, since the two words 'commands' and 'prohibits' indicate the establishment of the ruling, and as if justice, goodness, immorality, evil, and transgression are in one rank before the command and prohibition, and then they become differentiated by them. And this is other than customary good and evil (al-tahsin wa'l-taqbih al-'urfiyyan). As for the hadith, it is from the chapter of qiyas al-'aks (inverse analogy). Imam al-Razi said in al-Arba'in (1/350): 'The Mu'tazilites have agreed that the actions of Allah and His rulings are caused by considerations of the interests of the servants, and this is the choice of most of the later jurists, and this is false in our view.'

They also cite the hadith of Mu'adh where the Prophet indicates that lawful sexual relations can have reward, implying that the act itself has a moral quality before the ruling. The Ash'ari refutation is twofold. ?

Rational Proof for Hearing, Sight, and Speech
Sanusi provides a rational proof that Allah must possess hearing, sight, and speech.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational argument that proves Allah must possess hearing, sight, and speech.

Core Idea
A living being cannot be devoid of perfections without having their opposites, so Allah being perfect cannot have defects.

Sanusi presents a powerful rational proof for three of Allah's attributes: hearing, sight, and speech. The argument is based on the nature of living beings and the impossibility of defects in the divine. By reasoning from the necessity of either an attribute or its opposite for any living being, Sanusi concludes that Allah, the perfect Living, must possess these perfections.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Let the author's rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the logical structure: premise, deduction, conclusion.
2
Identify the key premise
The argument starts with a general principle about living beings. Identify that principle and how it applies to hearing, sight, and speech.
The premise is: every living being receptive to an attribute is not devoid of it or its like or its opposite.
3
Trace the conclusion
Follow the reasoning from the premise to the conclusion. Why must Allah have these attributes? Because lacking them would require their opposites, which are impossible for Him.
The conclusion is that Allah must possess hearing, sight, and speech.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( ويدلُّ على اتِّصافِهِ تعالى بهذهِ الثلاثة : العقل . . . ) إلى آخره ؛ يعني : أَنَّهُ يُستدَلُّ على ثبوتِ هذه الصفات الثلاث ـ وهي السمع والبصر والكلام - بالعقل ، والسمع وهو أولى
أما وجه الاستدلال عليها بالعقل : فهو أَنَّ كلَّ حيّ قابل لصفةٍ فَإِنَّهُ لا يخلو عنها أو عن مثلها أو عن ضدّها ، ولما وجدنا الحيَّ هو الذي يقبلُ الاتصاف بهذه الصفاتِ الثلاث ؛ بدليل امتناع اتصاف الميتِ بها .. وجبَ أنْ يكونَ المُصرِّحُ لقبولِها : إمَّا الحياةَ وإما أمراً يلازم الحياة ، وأياً ما كانَ يلزمُ عليهِ قبولُ اتِّصافِ كل حي بها ، فإذا لم يتّصف بها الحيُّ لزمَ أن يتّصفَ بأضدادِها ؛ وهي الصَّمَمُ والعمى والبَكَمُ ، لكنَّ هذهِ الأضداد في حقّهِ تعالى مستحيلة ؛ لكونها آفاتِ ونقائص ، وهو جلَّ وعزَّ مُنزَّه عنها بإجماع العقلاء ، فوجب أن يتّصفَ تعالى بتلك الكمالات
His saying: (And what indicates the description of the Most High with these three is reason...) to the end; means: that the establishment of these three attributes—hearing (al-samʿ), sight (al-baṣar), and speech (al-kalām)—is inferred by reason (al-ʿaql), and [inferred] by scripture (al-samʿ), the latter being superior. As for the way of inference by reason: it is that every living being that is receptive to an attribute is not devoid of it or of its like or of its opposite. And since we found that the living being is the one that accepts being described with these three attributes—as evidenced by the impossibility of a dead being being described with them—it becomes necessary that that which grants such acceptance is either life (al-ḥayāt) or something concomitant with life. Whichever it is, it necessarily follows that every living being can be described with them. So if the living being is not described with them, it must be described with their opposites, which are deafness (al-ṣamām), blindness (al-ʿamā), and muteness (al-bakam). But these opposites are impossible with respect to the Most High, because they are defects and deficiencies, and He, exalted and majestic, is transcendent above them by consensus of the rational people. Therefore it is necessary that the Most High be described with those perfections.
Source pages p. 311

Commentary
This passage is a proof (burhān aqlī) reasoning from the nature of living beings and the impossibility of defects for Allah. The argument proceeds as follows: every living being is such that for any attribute it can have, it either has that attribute, its like, or its opposite. Specifically, hearing, sight, and speech are attributes that only a living being can have—a dead being cannot have them. Therefore, the ground for their acceptance is either life itself or something inseparable from life. So every living being must be capable of having them. If a living being lacks them, it must have their opposites (deafness, blindness, muteness). Since Allah is the Living (al-Ḥayy), He cannot have these defective opposites, which are agreed to be imperfections. Therefore, He must possess the perfections of hearing, sight, and speech. Note that the text also mentions that scripture (al-samʿ) is a superior proof, but the rational proof is given first.

Key Terms
السمع
البصر
الكلام
الحياة
الصمم
العمى
البكم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that reason alone is insufficient to prove that Allah possesses hearing, sight, and speech.
Correction: This passage shows that a valid rational argument can be constructed based on the nature of living beings and the impossibility of defects in Allah.

Checkpoint
According to the rational proof, if a living being lacks hearing, sight, and speech, what must it have?
A) Nothing; it simply lacks them.
B) Their opposites: deafness, blindness, muteness.
C) Some other unrelated attributes.
D) It must not be alive.

Key Takeaway
The rational proof shows that Allah must possess hearing, sight, and speech because a perfect living being cannot have their opposites, which are defects.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You claim Allah hears every word you utter—including whispers in darkness. But do you live as if He does? When you say something in private, what would you change right now if you truly believed He was listening? Commit today to speak in a way that honors His hearing.
?
If seeing Allah's perfection requires seeing your own defects, what defects are you avoiding? The proof says Allah cannot be blind, but you might be blind to your own faults. Name one area where you have been refusing to see the truth, and ask Allah to open your eyes today.
?
You affirm Allah speaks—through revelation. But when was the last time you let His speech change your actions? This is not just belief; it is accountability. Will you choose one verse from your next reading to implement immediately, or are you content to merely acknowledge His speech without letting it speak into your life?

The Kalima: Negation and Affirmation
Sanusi explains the composition of the kalima and the general meaning of negation and affirmation of divinity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that 'La ilaha illa Allah' is composed of negation and affirmation, and that it negates divinity and its properties from all besides God while affirming them exclusively for Him.

Core Idea
The kalima is a declaration of divine uniqueness encompassing all attributes.

Sanusi begins by explaining that the word of tawhid is built on two pillars: negation and affirmation. He then unpacks what is being negated and affirmed, showing that it is not just a simple statement but a comprehensive theological claim. This lesson will guide you through that foundational understanding.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation to grasp the overall meaning.
Notice the repetition of 'except God' emphasising exclusivity.
2
Identify negation and affirmation
Identify the specific things that are negated from other than God and affirmed for Him. Make a list of each.
The negation covers eternity, necessity, and various transcendence attributes.
3
Reflect on implications
Consider what these negations and affirmations tell us about God's nature. How does this shape our understanding of tawhid?
These are not mere phrases but indicate a radical uniqueness.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأيضاً : فكلمة التوحيد - وهي : ( لا إله إلا الله ) لمَّا كَانَتْ مُركَّبَةً مِنْ نفي وإثباتِ ، ولا شك أنَّ الذي نُفِيَ عن غيرِ مولانا جلَّ وعز ، وأُثبِتَ لهُ تعالى على سبيل الحصر هو الألوهية وخواصها ، حتى يتضمَّنُ قولنا : ( لا إله إلا الله ) معنى : لا قديم في ذاتِهِ وصفاتِهِ إلا الله تعالى ، ولا واجبَ البقاء فيهما إلا الله جل وعلا ، ولا مخالف للحوادثِ كلّها إلا الله تعالى ؛ بمعنى : أَنَّهُ ليسَ بجِرْمٍ ولا قائم بالجِرْمِ ، ولا في جهةٍ مِنَ الجهات ولا له جهةٌ ، ولا يُكيَّفُ ولا يُتوهم ، ولا قائم بنفسِهِ - بمعنى : أَنَّهُ لا غني عن المحل والمخصّص - إلا الله جل وعزَّ ، ولا قادر على كل الممكناتِ بقدرةٍ قديمة إلا الله جل وعلا ، ولا عالم بما لا يتناهى مِنَ المعلوماتِ بعلمٍ واحدٍ قديم إلا الله جلَّ وعزّ ، وقِسٌ على هذا جميع ما عرفت وجوبَهُ لمولانا جل وعزَّ ، ولهذا قالوا : حقيقة التوحيد : اعتقاد عدم الشريكِ في الألوهية وخواصها .. كانَ اللائق في الترتيب أنْ يُبَيِّنَ أَوَّلاً ما يُعرَفُ به وجود إله العالَمِ ، ثم ما يليقُ أنْ يتّصفَ بِهِ ، ثم بعد ذلكَ يُبَيِّنُ أَنَّ الذي عُرفَ وجوبُ اتِّصافِهِ بتلك الصفاتِ يستحيل أن يكونَ مُتعدّداً ، بل لا يمكن أن يكون إلا واحداً ، فلهذا قدَّمنا نحنُ إثباتَ أُلوهِيَّةِ مولانا جل وعزَّ وإثبات خواصها ، ثم شرعنا في هذا الباب في بيانِ انفرادِهِ تعالى بذلكَ
And also: the word of tawhid – which is 'La ilaha illa Allah' – since it is composed of negation and affirmation, and there is no doubt that what is negated from other than our Master, Exalted and Majestic, and affirmed for Him exclusively, is al-uluhiyya (divinity) and its properties, such that our saying 'La ilaha illa Allah' includes the meaning: there is no eternal in essence and attributes except God, and no necessary of existence in them except God, and no one contrary to all accidents except God – meaning that He is not a body nor a substratum, nor in any direction, nor has a direction, nor can be qualified or imagined, nor is He self-subsistent in the sense of not needing a place and a specifier – except God, and no one powerful over all possibles with an eternal power except God, and no one knowing infinite things with a single eternal knowledge except God. And compare to this all that you have known to be obligatory for our Master. Therefore they said: the reality of tawhid is the belief in the absence of a partner in divinity and its properties. It was appropriate in the order that one first explain that by which the existence of the God of the world is known, then what is befitting for Him to be described with, then after that explain that He who is known to be necessarily described with those attributes cannot be multiple, but must be one. For this reason, we first presented the proof of the divinity of our Master and the proof of its properties, then we began in this chapter to explain His exclusivity in that.
Source pages p. 344

Commentary
This passage explains the meaning of the kalima 'La ilaha illa Allah'. The author notes that it is composed of negation and affirmation. The negation removes al-uluhiyya (divinity) and its properties from anything other than God, while the affirmation restricts them exclusively to Him. The author then unpacks the implications: the kalima negates any other eternal being, any other necessary existent in essence and attributes, and any being that is not subject to accidents. It then explains God's transcendence: He is not a body, not a substratum, not in or having a direction, not qualifiable or imaginable, and not self-subsistent in the sense of needing a place and a specifier. The kalima also affirms that only God has eternal power over all possibles and eternal knowledge of all infinite things. The author concludes by stating that the proper order is to first prove God's existence, then His attributes, then His oneness, which is why they arranged the book accordingly.

Key Terms
توحيد
إله
ألوهية
نفي
إثبات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The kalima only negates the existence of other gods.
Correction: The kalima negates all divine attributes from others and affirms them exclusively for God, including eternity, transcendence, power, and knowledge.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what does the kalima negate from other than God?
A) Only existence
B) Only power
C) Divinity and its properties
D) Only creation

Key Takeaway
The kalima 'La ilaha illa Allah' declares that all divine attributes are exclusive to God alone.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite 'La ilaha illa Allah', do you truly internalize that there is no eternal being besides Allah? How does this affect your reliance on things that will pass away?
?
If Allah is not a body, not in a direction, and cannot be imagined, how does this challenge the mental image you may have harbored when supplicating? Are you willing to let go of that image to worship Him as He truly is?
?
Only Allah has power over all possibles and knows all infinite things. In what area of your life are you still acting as if someone else has ultimate control? What step can you take today to transfer that trust exclusively to Allah?

The Reality of Tawhid and the Order of Proof
Sanusi defines the reality of tawhid and outlines the logical order of proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the proper order for establishing tawhid and the definition of its reality.

Core Idea
True tawhid begins with proving God's existence, then His attributes, then His oneness.

After explaining the content of the kalima, Sanusi turns to a meta-reflection: what is the proper sequence for teaching tawhid? He states that one should first prove the existence of God, then His attributes, then His oneness. This lesson covers that methodological insight and the definition of tawhid.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation. Focus on the definition of tawhid and the three-step order.
The order is: existence → attributes → oneness.
2
Understand the three parts
Identify each of the three steps: what to establish first, second, third. Why is this order logical?
You cannot establish oneness without first knowing what attributes are being affirmed.
3
Apply to the broader text
Relate this methodological note to the overall structure of the book: the author first proved God and His attributes, and now in this chapter proves His oneness.
This shows the author follows his own recommended order.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأيضاً : فكلمة التوحيد - وهي : ( لا إله إلا الله ) لمَّا كَانَتْ مُركَّبَةً مِنْ نفي وإثباتِ ، ولا شك أنَّ الذي نُفِيَ عن غيرِ مولانا جلَّ وعز ، وأُثبِتَ لهُ تعالى على سبيل الحصر هو الألوهية وخواصها ، حتى يتضمَّنُ قولنا : ( لا إله إلا الله ) معنى : لا قديم في ذاتِهِ وصفاتِهِ إلا الله تعالى ، ولا واجبَ البقاء فيهما إلا الله جل وعلا ، ولا مخالف للحوادثِ كلّها إلا الله تعالى ؛ بمعنى : أَنَّهُ ليسَ بجِرْمٍ ولا قائم بالجِرْمِ ، ولا في جهةٍ مِنَ الجهات ولا له جهةٌ ، ولا يُكيَّفُ ولا يُتوهم ، ولا قائم بنفسِهِ - بمعنى : أَنَّهُ لا غني عن المحل والمخصّص - إلا الله جل وعزَّ ، ولا قادر على كل الممكناتِ بقدرةٍ قديمة إلا الله جل وعلا ، ولا عالم بما لا يتناهى مِنَ المعلوماتِ بعلمٍ واحدٍ قديم إلا الله جلَّ وعزّ ، وقِسٌ على هذا جميع ما عرفت وجوبَهُ لمولانا جل وعزَّ ، ولهذا قالوا : حقيقة التوحيد : اعتقاد عدم الشريكِ في الألوهية وخواصها .. كانَ اللائق في الترتيب أنْ يُبَيِّنَ أَوَّلاً ما يُعرَفُ به وجود إله العالَمِ ، ثم ما يليقُ أنْ يتّصفَ بِهِ ، ثم بعد ذلكَ يُبَيِّنُ أَنَّ الذي عُرفَ وجوبُ اتِّصافِهِ بتلك الصفاتِ يستحيل أن يكونَ مُتعدّداً ، بل لا يمكن أن يكون إلا واحداً ، فلهذا قدَّمنا نحنُ إثباتَ أُلوهِيَّةِ مولانا جل وعزَّ وإثبات خواصها ، ثم شرعنا في هذا الباب في بيانِ انفرادِهِ تعالى بذلكَ
And also: the word of tawhid – which is 'La ilaha illa Allah' – since it is composed of negation and affirmation, and there is no doubt that what is negated from other than our Master, Exalted and Majestic, and affirmed for Him exclusively, is al-uluhiyya (divinity) and its properties, such that our saying 'La ilaha illa Allah' includes the meaning: there is no eternal in essence and attributes except God, and no necessary of existence in them except God, and no one contrary to all accidents except God – meaning that He is not a body nor a substratum, nor in any direction, nor has a direction, nor can be qualified or imagined, nor is He self-subsistent in the sense of not needing a place and a specifier – except God, and no one powerful over all possibles with an eternal power except God, and no one knowing infinite things with a single eternal knowledge except God. And compare to this all that you have known to be obligatory for our Master. Therefore they said: the reality of tawhid is the belief in the absence of a partner in divinity and its properties. It was appropriate in the order that one first explain that by which the existence of the God of the world is known, then what is befitting for Him to be described with, then after that explain that He who is known to be necessarily described with those attributes cannot be multiple, but must be one. For this reason, we first presented the proof of the divinity of our Master and the proof of its properties, then we began in this chapter to explain His exclusivity in that.
Source pages p. 344

Commentary
This passage explains the meaning of the kalima 'La ilaha illa Allah'. The author notes that it is composed of negation and affirmation. The negation removes al-uluhiyya (divinity) and its properties from anything other than God, while the affirmation restricts them exclusively to Him. The author then unpacks the implications: the kalima negates any other eternal being, any other necessary existent in essence and attributes, and any being that is not subject to accidents. It then explains God's transcendence: He is not a body, not a substratum, not in or having a direction, not qualifiable or imaginable, and not self-subsistent in the sense of needing a place and a specifier. The kalima also affirms that only God has eternal power over all possibles and eternal knowledge of all infinite things. The author concludes by stating that the proper order is to first prove God's existence, then His attributes, then His oneness, which is why they arranged the book accordingly.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Tawhid is simply saying 'La ilaha illa Allah' without any rational proof.
Correction: The reality of tawhid is a belief based on a logical sequence of proofs: existence, attributes, oneness.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, what should be proven first in establishing tawhid?
A) God's oneness
B) God's existence
C) God's attributes
D) God's power

Key Takeaway
Tawhid is not merely a statement; it is a rationally grounded belief built on proving God's existence, attributes, and oneness in that order.

?
Sanusi emphasizes a logical order in proving tawhid. In your own journey of faith, are you following that order? If not, what step have you neglected? Commit to studying one aspect of God's existence or attributes this week to strengthen your tawhid.

Proof Against Composition in God's Essence
Sanusi argues against conjunct multiplicity in God's essence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational proof that God's essence cannot be composed of parts.

Core Idea
A composite essence would lead to a body or originated attributes.

Sanusi begins by establishing that the oneness of God's essence is rationally provable. He argues that if God's essence were composed of parts (conjunct multiplicity), it would either be a body or lead to contradictions regarding divine attributes. Read the passage to trace the logical steps.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation. Notice that Sanusi presents two possible scenarios for a composite God.
The passage uses conditional reasoning: 'if... then...'.
2
Identify the two scenarios
The passage considers: (1) all parts bear divine attributes, (2) only one part bears them. Note the consequence of each.
The first leads to multiple gods; the second to a non-divine eternal entity.
3
Understand the specifying agent argument
Even if only one part has attributes, why would that part be chosen? This requires a specifying agent, making attributes originated.
This refutes the second scenario by showing it contradicts God's pre-eternity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أمَّا وَحدانية الذاتِ : فبرهانُها : أنَّهُ لو وقع التعدُّدُ فيها : فإِنْ كَانَ متصلاً لزمَ كونُ الذاتِ جسماً ; إذْ لا معنى للجسم إلا المركَّبُ مِنْ جزأين فأكثر . وأيضاً : فلو وقع التعدُّدُ في ذاتِ الإله ; بأن يتركَّبَ مِنْ جزأين فأكثر .. لم يخلُ : إمَّا أن تقوم صفاتُ الألوهية ; مِنَ القدرةِ والإرادة والعلم العامة التعلقِ ، ونحوها مِنْ صفاتِ الإله.. بكل جزءٍ مِنْ أجزاء الإله المفروض تركَّبُهُ ، أو تقومَ تلكَ الصفاتُ بجزء واحد . والأوَّلُ مستلزم لأنْ يكونَ كلُّ جزء إلهاً مستقلاً ، وذلك محالٌ ; لما ستعرفُ مِنْ برهان استحالة تعدد الآلهة (١) . والثاني يستلزم أن يكون ذلك الجزء الذي قامَتْ به صفاتُ الألوهية وحده هو الإله ، ويكون الجزء الآخرُ ذاتاً قديمة وليست بالله ، وقد عرفت فيما سبق أن لا قديمَ مِنَ الذواتِ إلا الله تعالى . وأيضاً : فاختصاص أحدِ الجزأين بأن يكون محلاً لصفاتِ الألوهية دونَ الآخر المماثل له .. يوُجِبُ الاحتياج إلى الفاعل المخصّص فتكون تلك الصفات حادثة ، وقد عرفت فيما سبق وجوب قدمِ الإله ووجوب قدم صفاته . وبمثل هذا تعرفُ استحالة التعدُّدِ المنفصل في ذات الإله ; لأنَّه لو كانَ ثَمَّ ذات أخرى مثلُها لم يخلُ أيضاً : إمَّا أَنْ تَتَّصفَ بمثلِ صفاتِها فيلزم تعدُّد الإله ، وسيأتي برهان بطلانه(۲) ، أو لا تتصف بمثل ذلكَ ، فيلزم احتياج صفاتِ الإلـه إلى المخصص ، ويلزم الحدوث على ما عرفت فيما مضى . قوله : ( وليس معنى نفي التركيب ... ) إلى آخره : إنَّما ذكر هذا الكلام دفعاً لما يُتوهَّمُ مِنْ أنَّ المراد بنفي التركيب في ذاته تعالى التناهي في الدقةِ كما هو معنى نفي التركيب في الجوهر الفردِ ، فنبَّهَ
As for the oneness of essence: its proof: that if multiplicity occurred in it, if it were conjunct, it would necessitate that the essence be a body, since there is no meaning of body except it is composed of two or more parts. Also: if multiplicity occurred in the essence of God, by its being composed of two or more parts, it would not be free: either the attributes of divinity—of power, will, and universal knowledge, and similar attributes of God—subsist in every part of the assumed composite parts of God, or those attributes subsist in one part. The first necessitates that every part be an independent god, and that is impossible, because of what you will know from the proof of the impossibility of multiplicity of gods. The second necessitates that the part in which the attributes of divinity subsist alone is God, and the other part is an ancient essence not God, and you have already learned in the foregoing that no essence is ancient except Allah Almighty. Also: the specification of one of the two parts to be a locus for the attributes of divinity to the exclusion of the other similar to it necessitates the need for a specifying agent (al-fa'il al-mukhassis), so those attributes would be originated (haditha), and you have already learned in the foregoing the necessity of the pre-eternity of God and the necessity of the pre-eternity of His attributes. And by similar reasoning you know the impossibility of disjunct multiplicity in the essence of God; because if there were another essence like it, it would also not be free: either it is described with the like of its attributes, then the multiplicity of gods would follow, and the proof of its falsity will come; or it is not described with the like of that, then the need of the attributes of God for a specifying agent follows, and origination (huduth) follows, as you have learned previously. His saying: 'And the meaning of negating composition is not...' to the end: He only mentioned this speech to repel what might be imagined, that the intended meaning by negating composition in His essence, exalted, is fineness in subtlety, as is the meaning of negating composition in the indivisible atom (al-jawhar al-fard), so he alerted.
Source pages p. 355

Commentary
This passage provides rational proofs for the oneness of essence (wahdaniyyat al-dhat). It begins by arguing against conjunct multiplicity (composition): if God's essence were composed of parts, it would be a body, which is impossible. Then it considers two possibilities for attributes subsisting in a composite God. First, if all parts have divine attributes, then each part is a separate god, which is absurd. Second, if only one part has divine attributes, then the other part is an ancient entity not God, contradicting the uniqueness of the eternal. Additionally, if one part is chosen over another for attributes, that requires a specifying agent, making the attributes originated, but God and His attributes are pre-eternal. Then the proof extends to disjunct multiplicity (separate gods): if another essence similar to God existed, it either shares divine attributes (leading to multiple gods) or does not (making God's attributes need a specifying agent, again implying origination). Lastly, the author clarifies that negating composition does not mean the divine essence is an indivisible atom (jawhar fard) in terms of fineness; it means it is not composed of parts. Thus, the oneness of essence is rationally established.

التعدد المتصل
التركيب
الجسم
الفاعل المخصص

In Sanusi's proof against composition in God's essence, what is one consequence if only one part of a supposed composite God bears the divine attributes?
A) The other part would be a second god

C) Both parts would be gods
D) The attributes would be eternal

Key Takeaway
God's essence cannot be composed of parts because composition would either produce multiple gods or originated attributes.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In your daily life, do you ever think of God's attributes as if they were separate 'parts' of Him, such as 'His mercy here, His justice there'? How does the proof that His essence is not composite challenge that tendency? What step will you take today to unify your understanding of His attributes in your worship?
?
If you truly internalize that God's essence cannot be composed, how does that affect the way you respond to trials? Can you trust that all His attributes—power, will, knowledge—are perfectly unified in every situation? What does that demand of you when you feel life is fragmented?
?
The proof shows that composition leads to either multiple gods or originated attributes. When you find yourself complaining about God's decree, are you implicitly assuming a 'part' of God is missing or insufficient? What concrete action can you take to remind yourself of His simple, undivided essence in moments of doubt?

Proof Against Separate Multiplicity and Clarification
Sanusi argues against separate multiplicity and clarifies negation of composition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the proof that there cannot be multiple gods (disjunct multiplicity) and why negating composition does not mean God is an indivisible atom.

Core Idea
Multiple gods would either share attributes (contradiction) or require a specifying agent.

Sanusi extends his proof to disjunct multiplicity—the idea of multiple separate gods. He shows that if another essence like God existed, it would either share divine attributes or not, both leading to impossibilities. He then clarifies that negating composition does not reduce God to an indivisible atom. Read the passage to see the logic.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation. Notice the parallel structure with the previous proof.
The argument mirrors the conjunct case but with separate essences.
2
Identify the two possibilities for a second essence
The passage considers: either the second essence is described with the same attributes or not. Trace each outcome.
If same attributes → multiple gods (absurd). If not → attributes need a specifying agent (contingent).
3
Understand the clarification
The last sentence explains that negating composition in God does not mean He is like an indivisible atom (jawhar fard). It simply means He has no parts.
This prevents a misunderstanding that might arise from similar terminology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

As for the oneness of essence: its proof: that if multiplicity occurred in it, if it were conjunct, it would necessitate that the essence be a body, since there is no meaning of body except it is composed of two or more parts. Rational and Revealed Proofs for Acquisition (Kasb)
Sanusi enumerates two proofs for kasb, focusing on the rational argument comparing voluntary and involuntary movements.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two proofs—revealed and rational—that the Ash'ari school uses to establish the doctrine of kasb (acquisition) for human actions.

Core Idea
The rational proof shows that voluntary acts differ from involuntary ones due to a contingent power that accompanies the act without creating it.

Sanusi now turns to defending the central Ash'ari doctrine of kasb. He provides two lines of evidence: one from divine law and one from reason itself. The rational argument is especially subtle—it forces us to locate the difference between a trembling hand and a hand raised by choice, even when the physical motion is identical.

Guided Path
1
Understand the definition of kasb
Read the opening where Sanusi defines kasb as the accompaniment of a contingent power to a voluntary action without effect. This is crucial for the proofs.
The power does not cause the action; it merely accompanies it.
2
Examine the revealed proof
Notice that the revealed proof is simply that the Law (shar') only obligates acquired acts. Reflect on why this is a valid theological evidence.
Sanusi only alludes to it; the earlier lesson likely elaborated.
3
Analyze the rational proof step by step
Follow the logical argument: we perceive a necessary distinction between involuntary and voluntary movements. Assume two physically identical movements—one involuntary, one voluntary. The difference cannot be in the movement itself or the mover's essence. Therefore it must be due to something additional: the contingent power (kasb).
The argument is a 'sabr' (investigation) of possible causes.
4
Connect to the broader Ash'ari position
Understand how this argument preserves God's sole creative power while still attributing the act to the human. The contingent power is a 'property' that makes the act acquired, not created.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( والذي يدلُّ على مصاحبة هذه القدرة الحادثة للفعل ... ) إلى آخرِهِ ؛ يعني : أنَّ أهلَ الحقِّ استدلُّوا على ثبوتِ الكسب للعبدِ ؛ بمعنى : أنَّ فعلَهُ الاختياري ـ أي : الذي يصح منه في العادة تركه وفعلُهُ - تصاحبه عند وجودِهِ فيهِ قدرةٌ حادثةٌ تتعلَّقُ بهِ مِنْ غير تأثير لها فيه أصلاً . . بدليلين أحدهما : شرعيٌّ : وقد أشار إليه فيما سبق ؛ وهو أنَّ الشرعَ إنَّما كلَّفَ بالمكتسب مِنَ الأفعالِ دون غيرها . الثاني : عقلي : وهو ما أشرنا إليه هنا مِنْ إدراكنا الفَرْقَ ضرورةً بين حركة الاضطرارِ ؛ كحركةِ الرَّعْشَةِ أو تحريك الغيرِ يدَنا ونحوِ ذلك ، وبين حركة الاختيار ؛ وهي الحركة التي يتمكَّنُ عادةً مِنْ فعلها وتركها ولنفرض هاتين الحركتين متحدتين في الجهة والحيز حتى يتماثلا ، فنقولُ في سَبْرِ سببِ الفرقِ الضروري بينهما : لا يصح أنْ ترجعَ التفرقة بينهما إلى نفس الحركة وحقيقتها ؛ لفَرْضِ تماثلهما ، ولا إلى نفس ذاتِ المتحرِّكِ ؛ لأنَّ معقول ذاتِهِ في الحالتين واحدٌ
His saying: 'And what indicates the accompaniment of this contingent power to the action...' to the end of it means: that the People of Truth (ahl al-haqq) have deduced the establishment of acquisition (kasb) for the servant; meaning that his voluntary action—i.e., that which it is normally possible for him to leave and do—is accompanied, at its existence in him, by a contingent power that relates to it without having any effect on it at all. By two evidences: One is revealed (shar'i): He alluded to it previously; that the Law obligated only the acquired actions to the exclusion of others. The second is rational ('aqli): which we alluded to here from our necessary perception of the distinction between involuntary movement (harakat al-idtirar)—like the movement of tremble or another moving our hand and the like—and voluntary movement (harakat al-ikhtiyar), which is the movement that one normally can do and leave. Let us suppose these two movements unified in direction and space so that they become identical; then we say in investigating the cause of the necessary difference between them: It is not valid that the distinction between them goes back to the movement itself and its essence, because we suppose them to be identical; nor to the very essence of the mover, because the intelligible of his essence is one in both states.
Source pages p. 379

Commentary
This passage provides the proof for the Ash'ari doctrine of kasb (acquisition). The author first defines kasb: that the voluntary act is accompanied by a contingent power (qudra haditha) that relates to it without causing it. Then he gives two evidences. The revealed evidence is that the Law (shar') only obligates actions that are acquired (muktasab) by the servant, not those beyond his power. The rational evidence is based on the necessary distinction we perceive between involuntary and voluntary movements. For example, a trembling hand (involuntary) vs. a hand deliberately raised. Even if we imagine two movements identical in all physical respects—same direction, same space—we still necessarily distinguish them. This distinction cannot be due to the movement itself (since they are postulated identical) nor to the mover's essence (the person's self is same). Therefore, the distinction must be due to something additional in the voluntary case, which is the contingent power (qudra) that accompanies the action without affecting its reality. This power is the 'acquisition' (kasb) that makes the action attributable to the servant while God remains the sole creator of the action. The argument is a careful logical analysis to locate the difference between compelled and free acts.

Key Terms
كسب
قدرة حادثة
فعل اختياري
حركة اضطرار
حركة اختيار
دليل شرعي
دليل عقلي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that the contingent power (qudra haditha) creates the action or that the human is the true agent.
Correction: In Ash'ari theology, the contingent power merely accompanies the action without any effect; God alone creates all actions. The human's 'acquisition' (kasb) makes the action morally attributable to them.

Checkpoint
According to the rational evidence, why does the necessary distinction between involuntary and voluntary movement not refer to the movement itself?
A) Because the two movements are not identical.
B) Because we suppose them identical in direction and space.
C) Because the mover's essence differs.
D) Because the Law distinguishes them.

Key Takeaway
The rational proof for kasb shows that voluntary acts are distinguished from involuntary ones not by the movement itself or the agent's essence, but by an accompanying contingent power that makes the act acquired.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You just learned that every voluntary action you take is accompanied by a power from Allah that does not create it but makes it 'yours.' Think of one decision you made today—raising your hand, speaking, or choosing a task. In that moment, did you feel the weight of Allah's sole creativity, or did you assume you were the independent cause? How can you train yourself to see your actions as acquired rather than produced?
?
The rational proof showed that even if two movements are physically identical, one can be forced and the other free. Where in your life have you blamed circumstances or Allah for something you truly acquired? What would change if you fully owned your voluntary actions as your kasb while acknowledging Allah as their only real creator?
?
The distinction between involuntary and voluntary is 'necessarily perceived'—you know it instantly. Yet believers and non-believers both experience this distinction. What does this common human experience of free choice tell you about Allah's justice in holding you accountable? Will you stop hiding behind 'I had no choice' for sins you actually acquired? Commit to one specific area today where you will stop pretending you are forced.

The Sunni Middle Path on Human Actions
Sanusi defines the Sunni position on human actions, avoiding Jabriyya and Qadariyya.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Ash'ari doctrine balances divine omnipotence and human accountability by distinguishing voluntary and involuntary actions.

Core Idea
The Ash'ari position avoids fatalism and freewill extremes by affirming human capacity without effect.

Sanusi presents the Sunni creed on human actions, showing how it steers clear of two dangerous extremes. The people of truth combine rational reality with divine law, affirming that humans have a capacity for voluntary actions but that all effects belong to God alone. This lesson unpacks that delicate balance.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing, then read the literal translation. Let the author's own phrasing set the stage.
2
Identify how the Sunni position avoids Jabriyya
Look for the division of actions into voluntary and involuntary, and the phrase 'capacity without effect'. This is the key escape from fatalism.
Jabriyya claimed humans have no role at all.
3
Identify how it avoids Qadariyya
Notice the strong denial of any effect from the originated power. The servant, power, and act are all created by God directly.
Qadariyya claimed humans create their own acts.
4
Understand 'capacity without effect'
Reflect on the paradox: the servant has a power that accompanies the action but does not cause it. This preserves both accountability and divine omnipotence.
This is the Ash'ari doctrine of kasb (acquisition).
5
Connect to taklif (obligation)
Notice that voluntary actions are within the usual capacity of the accountable person, and obligation is based on them as per divine law.
This shows why humans are rewarded or punished.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أمَّا مذهب أهلِ الحقِّ رضيَ الله تعالى عنهم : فقد جمع بين الحقيقة والشريعة ، وسلم بفضْلِ اللهِ تعالى مِنْ بدعة الفريقين ؛ لأنَّهم جانبوا الجبرية ؛ بتقسيم الأفعالِ إلى قسمين : اختيارية واضطرارية ، وأنَّ الأولى مقدورة للعبدِ ؛ بمعنى : أنَّ لهُ قدرةً حادثة تقارن تلك الأفعال الاختيارية وتتعلَّقُ بها مِنْ غيرِ تأثير ، وهذه الأفعال هي التي في وسع المكلَّف عادةً ، وبها وقعَ التكليف على حسَبِ ما دلّ عليه الشرعُ . وجانبوا القدريَّةً ؛ لكونهم لم يجعلوا لتلك القدرةِ الحادثة تأثيراً ألبتة في أثر ما عموماً ، بل العبد عندَهم وقدرته الحادثة ومقدورُها الكل مخلوق الله تعالى بلا واسطة ولا شريك أصلاً ، على حسَبِ ما دلت عليه الحقيقة العقليَّةُ
As for the doctrine of the people of truth, may God be pleased with them: it combines between reality and law, and they were saved by God's grace from the innovation of the two factions; because they avoided the Jabriyya by dividing actions into two kinds: voluntary and involuntary, and that the first are within the capacity of the servant; meaning: he has an originated power that accompanies those voluntary actions and is related to them without any effect, and these actions are those within the usual ability of the accountable person, and by them obligation occurred according to what the law indicates. And they avoided the Qadariyya because they did not make for that originated power any effect at all in any effect generally, rather the servant, his originated power, and all that it is capable of are all created by God Almighty without intermediary and no partner at all, according to what the rational reality indicates.
Source pages p. 385

Commentary
This passage is a definition and explanation of the Sunni (Ash'ari) doctrine regarding human actions. Sanusi begins by stating that the Sunni position combines both reality (al-ḥaqīqa) and law (al-sharīʿa), thus avoiding the innovations of the two extreme factions. They avoid Jabriyya (fatalism) by dividing actions into voluntary (ikhtiyāriyya) and involuntary (iḍṭirāriyya). The voluntary ones are within the servant's capacity (maqdūra), meaning he has an originated power (qudra ḥāditha) that accompanies the action but has no effect (lā ta'thīr). These actions are what the accountable person can normally do, and obligation (taklīf) is based on them as the law indicates. They avoid Qadariyya (free will) by affirming that this originated power has absolutely no effect in producing any effect; rather, the servant, his power, and all he can do are all created by God directly without intermediary or partner, as rational reality requires.

Key Terms
أهل الحق
الحقيقة والشريعة
الأفعال الاختيارية والاضطرارية
قدرة حادثة
لا تأثير
وسع المكلف
التكليف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the Ash'ari doctrine denies human capacity altogether, claiming humans are completely passive.
Correction: The Ash'ari position affirms a real capacity (qudra ḥāditha) that accompanies voluntary actions, but this capacity has no creative effect; the action is still created by God.

Checkpoint
How do the people of truth avoid the innovation of the Jabriyya?
A) By denying all human actions
B) By dividing actions into voluntary and involuntary, and affirming capacity without effect
C) By affirming that humans create their own actions
D) By denying the existence of involuntary actions

Key Takeaway
The Sunni doctrine affirms human capacity for voluntary actions without granting any creative effect, preserving God's sole agency.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If your voluntary actions are accompanied by a power that has no creative effect, do you truly feel the weight of responsibility for your choices? In what area of your life do you tend to rely on your own ability rather than recognizing God as the sole creator of your actions? What one change can you make today to shift that reliance?
?
Knowing that the Sunni middle path avoids both fatalism and self-reliance, which extreme do you lean towards in your daily struggles? How can you actively embody the truth that you are accountable yet powerless, this very day?
?
If God creates all your actions—even your obedience and disobedience—how does that affect your gratitude for your good deeds and your repentance for your sins? Will you thank Him for your obedience and seek His forgiveness for your sins, acknowledging His sole agency?

The Quranic Evidence of God's Authority
Sanusi quotes Quranic verses rebuking disbelief.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Quranic verses cited by Sanusi establish God's absolute authority over disbelief and guidance.

Core Idea
The Quran repeatedly shames disbelief, showing God's sole authority over faith.

Sanusi begins his argument by citing several Quranic verses that rebuke disbelief. These verses serve as foundational proofs that human beings have no excuse for rejecting God's signs. They set the stage for the rational argument that follows.

Guided Path
1
Recite the Quranic verses
Read the Arabic verses Sanusi quotes and their translations. Notice how each verse questions the disbeliever's stance.
These verses are from Surah Al-Baqarah, Yunus, and Az-Zumar.
2
Identify the common theme
All verses rebuke disbelief and imply that only God can guide or misguide. Reflect on the message of each.
3
Understand the purpose
Sanusi uses these verses to ground the rational discussion in revelation. Recognize that the Quran repeatedly asserts God's absolute authority.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كَيْفَ تَكْفُرُونَ بِاللَّهِ ﴾ [البقرة : ۲۸] ، وقولِهِ تعالى : ﴿ فَأَنَّى تُؤْفَكُونَ ﴾ [يونس : ٣٤] ، فَأَنَّى تُصْرَفُونَ ﴾ [الزمر : ٦] ، ونحو ذلك مما هو كثير . وأما بحسَبِ ما دلَّ عليهِ العقلُ : فمرجعُ التكاليف كلّها إلى أنَّها أعلام مِنَ اللهِ تعالى بما جعلَ مِنْ أفعالِهِ بمخض اختياره أمارةً على الثواب ؛ كالواجباتِ والمندوباتِ ، أو على العقاب ؛ كالمحرَّماتِ ، أو ليسَ أمارةً على شيءٍ منها ؛ كالمباحاتِ والمكروهات ، والحكم بالسعادة والشقاوة أزلي لا سبب لهُ ، فالله سبحانه يحكم بما يشاء ، ويفعل ما يريدُ ، لا يُسأل عما يفعل ، فتبارك وتعالى (١) .
How do you disbelieve in Allah? [Quran 2:28], and His saying, Exalted is He: 'Then how are you deluded?' [Quran 10:34], 'Then how are you turned away?' [Quran 39:6], and the like of that which is abundant. And as for what the intellect indicates: the reference of all obligations is that they are signs (a‘lām) from Allah, Exalted is He, of what He has made from His acts, by the purest of His choice, an indicator of reward – like obligatory and recommended acts – or of punishment – like forbidden acts – or not an indicator of any of them – like permissible and disliked acts. And the judgment of happiness and misery is eternal, having no cause. So Allah, glorified and exalted, judges as He wills and does what He desires; He is not asked about what He does. So blessed and exalted is He.
Source pages p. 388

Commentary
This passage is a combined scriptural and rational argument establishing that all religious obligations (takālīf) from God function as signs (a‘lām) that point to reward or punishment, and that the ultimate decree of felicity or damnation is eternal and uncaused. The author begins by citing several Quranic verses that rebuke disbelief and imply God's absolute authority over guidance. Then, turning to rational argument, he states that the common purpose of all obligations is that they are signs from God: He has made certain acts – by His own choice – indicators of reward (like wajibāt and mandūbāt) or punishment (like muḥarramāt), or not indicators of either (like mubāḥāt and makrūhāt). Importantly, the passage then asserts that God's judgment of happiness or misery (sa‘ādah or shaqāwah) is eternal (azalī) and has no cause (lā sabab lahu). This means human actions do not cause God's decree; rather, the decree is prior and unconditional. God acts as He wills, is not questioned, and is exalted beyond all. The structure is: (1) Quranic evidence, (2) rational explanation of obligations as signs, (3) affirmation of the eternal, uncaused judgment. This guards against the false notion that human choices determine God's decree.

Key Terms
أعلام
التكاليف
الحكم بالسعادة والشقاوة
أزلي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) 2:28
B) 10:34
C) 39:6
D) 12:12

Key Takeaway
Quranic verses reveal that disbelief stems from ingratitude and delusion, highlighting God's authority over guidance.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read 'How do you disbelieve in Allah?', where in your own life do you find yourself turning away from acknowledging Allah's authority? What would it cost you to fully submit in that area?
?
The Quran asks 'Then how are you deluded?' What are the modern delusions that keep you from true faith? Are you willing to see them?
?
If Allah is challenging you directly through these verses, what is your honest response? Will you continue to turn away, or will you answer the call right now?

Obligations as Signs and the Eternal Decree
Sanusi rationally explains obligations as signs and the eternal decree.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Sanusi's rational argument that all religious obligations are signs from God indicating reward or punishment, and that God's eternal decree of happiness or misery has no cause.

Core Idea
Obligations are signs, not causes, of God's eternal, uncaused decree.

After citing Quranic verses, Sanusi turns to rational analysis. He explains that every religious obligation is a sign from God pointing to reward or punishment, and that God's judgment of who will be happy or miserable is eternal and without any cause. This is a foundational doctrine in Ash'ari theology regarding God's absolute sovereignty.

Guided Path
1
Understand the classification
Read how Sanusi divides obligations into three categories: indicators of reward, indicators of punishment, and indicators of neither. Identify examples for each.
Wajib and mandub indicate reward; haram indicates punishment; mubah and makruh indicate neither.
2
Grasp the eternal decree
Sanusi asserts that God's judgment of happiness or misery is eternal and uncaused. This means human actions do not cause the decree.
This rejects the notion that God's will is influenced by creation.
3
Reflect on God's absolute freedom
The passage concludes that God is not questioned about His actions. Consider how this establishes divine transcendence.

?

?

?

Al-Baqillani's View on Created Power's Effect
Sanusi warns against relying on other opinions, citing al-Baqillani's view.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the mainstream Sunni position that created power has absolutely no effect and be able to distinguish it from al-Baqillani's minority view that it affects the description of the act.

Core Idea
Created power has no effect; al-Baqillani's view is not the mainstream.

In this passage, Sanusi issues a warning about other opinions attributed to Ahl al-Sunnah that are not the relied-upon view. He reaffirms the mainstream position that created power has absolutely no effect, then cites al-Baqillani's opinion that it affects only the description of the act, not its existence. This lesson helps you navigate between the established creed and a notable dissenting view.

Guided Path
1
Read the warning passage
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice that Sanusi starts by emphasizing that the mainstream view is the only correct one.
The phrase 'ليس عليها المُعوَّلُ' indicates the other views are not reliable.
2
Identify the two views
Find the description of the mainstream view: created power has absolutely no effect. Then find al-Baqillani's view: it affects the most specific description of the act.
Contrast 'عدم التأثير ألبتة' with 'تُؤثر في أخص وصف الفعل'.
3
Understand the distinction in al-Baqillani's view
Al-Baqillani distinguishes between the existence of the act (which is from Allah) and its specific description (like being prayer or theft), which he says is affected by created power.
This is a subtle point: the power does not create, but it 'specifies' the act type.
4
Grasp the warning's purpose
Sanusi is cautioning students not to mistake al-Baqillani's view for the mainstream Ahl al-Sunnah position. The warning prevents confusion in creed.
The mention of al-Taftazani shows this view is known but not relied upon.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تنبیه: على أقوال أعلام مِنْ أهل السنَّةِ ليس عليها المُعوَّلُ ] ما اقتصرنا عليه في أصلِ العقيدةِ مِنْ عدم التأثير للقدرة الحادثة ألبتة هو المعروفُ المشهورُ عندَهم، الذي لا يصح عقلاً ولا شرعاً خلافه، وبعضُ مَنْ أُولعَ بنقل الغثّ والسمينِ مِنَ الأقوال .. ينقلُ هنا أقوالاً أُخَرَ ينسبها لأهل السنَّةِ أيضاً. فمنها ما نُقِلَ عن القاضي أبي بكر الباقلاني أنَّ القدرة الحادثةَ تُؤثر في أخص وصف الفعل؛ ككونه صلاةً أو غَصْباً أو زناً أو نحو ذلك، لا في وجود أصل الفعل، هكذا مَثَلَ الأخص التفتازاني في ( شرح المقاصدِ الدينيَّة ) له
Warning: Regarding the sayings of some eminent figures of Ahl al-Sunnah that are not the relied upon [views]: What we have confined ourselves to in the original creed, that the created power has absolutely no effect, is the well-known and famous [view] among them, the opposite of which is not valid rationally or legally. But some who are fond of transmitting the worthless and the valuable of sayings... transmit here other sayings that they attribute to Ahl al-Sunnah as well. Among them is what is transmitted from al-Qadi Abu Bakr al-Baqillani that the created power has an effect on the most specific description of the act, such as it being prayer or usurpation or fornication or the like, not on the existence of the act itself. Thus al-Taftazani gave an example of the most specific in his commentary on al-Maqasid al-Diniyyah.
Source pages p. 390

Commentary
This passage is a warning (tanbih) about other opinions that are sometimes attributed to Ahl al-Sunnah but are not the relied-upon view. The author reiterates that the mainstream Sunni position is that created power has absolutely no effect (on the existence of an action). He then cites one such dissenting opinion: that of al-Qadi Abu Bakr al-Baqillani. Al-Baqillani held that while created power does not bring about the existence of the act, it does affect the specific description or nature of the act — whether it is an act of obedience, transgression, etc. Al-Taftazani in his commentary on al-Maqasid al-Diniyyah mentions this as an example of the 'most specific' distinction. The author is not endorsing this view; rather, he is warning that it is not the relied-upon position.

Key Terms
القدرة الحادثة
تأثير
أخص وصف الفعل
القاضي أبو بكر الباقلاني
التفتازاني

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that al-Baqillani's view is the standard Ahl al-Sunnah position, or that created power can bring about the existence of actions.
Correction: The passage clarifies that the mainstream view is that created power has absolutely no effect, and al-Baqillani's view is a dissenting opinion that only affects the description, not existence.

Checkpoint
According to al-Baqillani's view as cited, what does the created power affect?
A) The existence of the act
B) The most specific description of the act (e.g., being obedience or sin)
C) Both existence and description
D) Neither

Key Takeaway
The mainstream Sunni position is that created power has no effect; al-Baqillani's view that it affects only the description of the act is a minority opinion not relied upon in creed.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you learn that a great scholar like al-Baqillani held a view that seems more 'reasonable' to you, do you feel a pull to adopt it? What does that reveal about your attachment to your own intellect versus submission to the relied-upon consensus of Ahl al-Sunnah? Will you actively check your inclinations and defer to the mainstream position?
?
This passage warns against transmitting 'the worthless and the valuable' indiscriminately. Have you ever shared a religious opinion without verifying its authority, simply because it came from a respected name? Will you commit to only transmitting what is relied upon, even if it feels less exciting?
?
Imagine you are tempted to believe that your own effort or power affects the moral quality of your deeds—that you can, by your own choice, make an act good or evil. How does this passage challenge that assumption? Are you willing to let go of the pride that whispers your contribution matters, and accept that all power belongs to Allah alone?

Ruling on Differences in Doctrinal vs. Legal Matters
Author distinguishes doctrinal matters from legal ones regarding ijtihad and reward.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the critical difference between doctrinal and legal matters in terms of ijtihad, sin, and reward, and the importance of sincerity in seeking truth.

Core Idea
Doctrinal truth is singular; error leads to hell. Legal debates are rewarded even when wrong.

This passage from Sanusi lays down a foundational distinction: not all scholarly disagreement is treated equally. Before diving into specific creedal issues, we must understand when ijtihad is permissible and when it is not. The author contrasts the leniency in legal matters with the strictness in doctrinal ones, and then draws a powerful conclusion about the seeker's intention.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without pausing. Then read the translation. Notice the shift in tone between the two types of matters.
The passage has two clear sections: legal vs. doctrinal, then a motivational conclusion.
2
Identify the two categories
Find the parts that describe legal matters (where ijtihad is valid) and doctrinal matters (where only one correct view exists). Note the difference in reward and punishment.
Legal matters are called 'أخطاء ونحوها' (errors and the like). Doctrinal matters are called 'العقليات'.
3
Understand the consensus on doctrinal matters
Focus on the phrase 'الإجماع على أن المصيب فيها واحد' (consensus that the one correct is one). This is the key point. Note that ignorance or ijtihad does not excuse.
4
Reflect on the motivational conclusion
The author describes two types of seekers: sincere and insincere. Notice how sincerity leads to divine help, while pride leads to deprivation.
The Quranic verse (7:146) is cited to emphasize this.
5
Apply the distinction
Think of a contemporary example: should all opinions on Allah's attributes be considered equally valid? The passage says no.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أخطاً ونحوها ، التي لا يجب فيها تعيينُ مذهبٍ مُعيَّن للاتباع ، ولا إثم فيهِ على مجتهد مِنَ المجتهدين ، بل كلُّهم مأجورٌ ; مَنْ أَصَابَ منهم ومَنْ ، وقد قيل : إنَّهم كلَّهم مصيبونَ (١) ، أما العقليَّاتُ فالإجماع على أنَّ المصيب فيها واحدٌ ، وأنَّ المخالف للحقِّ في عقائدِ الإيمانِ مخطى آثم ، مُخلَّدٌ في النارِ ، اجتهد أو قلَّدَ ، لا يُعذَرُ فيها بالجهل ولا بغيره (۲) وحاصل الأمر : أَنَّ مَنْ كانَتْ همَّتُهُ البحث عن الحقِّ للفوز برضوان الله تعالى ، وإنقاذ مهجتِهِ مِنْ سخط مولاه جل وعزَّ . . فإنَّ اللهَ تعالى بفضلِهِ يعينُهُ ويُبلِّغُهُ أملَهُ ، وينقذُهُ وينقذُ بِهِ مَنِ اقتدى بهديهِ مِنَ المهالك وأَمَّا مَنْ كانَ الهوى قائدَ علمِهِ ، ونيتُهُ الظهور ، والتكاثر وجذْبُ القلوبِ التي لا تنفع ولا تضرُّ مقصدَهُ ، والدعوة العريضة الدالة على سخافة عقله وعظيم جهلِهِ معظم أمرِهِ .. فإِنَّ العَالَبَ مِنْ عادةِ اللهِ تعالى ألا يُمكِّنَ قلبَهُ مِنْ نورٍ ، ولا مِنْ تحقيق لعلم نافع ، وإن جرى مُجرَّدُ حروفه على لسانِهِ ، سَأَصْرِفُ عَنْ ءَايَتِيَ الَّذِينَ يَتَكَبَّرُونَ فِي الْأَرْضِ بِغَيْرِ الْحَقِّ ﴾ [الأعراف : ١٤٦] ، وهلاك هذا وهلاكُ مَنِ اقتدى بهِ هو الأغلبُ ، إلا أنْ يتداركه المولى جل وعزَّ بِسَعَةِ رَحمتِهِ وجميل عَفْوِهِ اللهم ; اغفر لنا ما مضى ، وتُبْ علينا ، وأصلحنا فيما بَقِيَ إلى المماتِ ، يا أرحم الراحمين .
Error and the like, in which it is not obligatory to specify a particular school for following, and there is no sin therein upon a mujtahid among the mujtahids, rather all of them are rewarded: whoever is correct among them and whoever [errs?], and it has been said: they are all correct (1). As for rational matters, there is consensus that the one correct is one, and that the one who opposes the truth in the beliefs of faith is erring and sinful, eternally in the Fire, whether he exerted effort or imitated, he is not excused therein by ignorance nor by other than it (2). The upshot of the matter: that whoever's concern is the search for truth to gain the pleasure of Allah the Exalted, and to rescue his soul from the wrath of his Master, Majestic and Mighty... then Allah the Exalted by His favor helps him and delivers him to his hope, and delivers him and by him delivers whoever follows his guidance from the perils. And as for the one whose guide of his knowledge is passion, and his intention is ostentation, and accumulation, and attracting hearts that neither benefit nor harm his purpose, and the broad call indicative of the foolishness of his mind and the greatness of his ignorance in most of his affair... then the usual way of Allah the Exalted is that He does not give his heart light, nor any realization of beneficial knowledge, even if mere letters flow on his tongue. 'I will turn away from My signs those who are arrogant upon the earth without right' [Al-A'raf 7:146]. The destruction of this one and the destruction of whoever follows him is the most frequent, except that the Lord, Majestic and Mighty, overtakes him with the vastness of His mercy and beautiful pardon. O Allah, forgive us what has passed, and turn to us, and reform us in what remains until death, O Most Merciful of the merciful.
Source pages p. 400

Commentary
This passage begins by addressing issues where ijtihad is permissible, specifically matters that are not doctrinal. It states that in such matters, there is no requirement to follow a specific school, and no sin upon a mujtahid; rather all mujtahids are rewarded, whether correct or in error, and some even say all are correct. Then it sharply contrasts doctrinal matters ('al-aqliyat'), where there is consensus that only one position is correct, and the one who opposes the truth in matters of faith is both erring and sinful, and will be eternally in Hellfire, whether he performed ijtihad or followed blind imitation. Ignorance does not excuse such a person. The author then draws the practical conclusion: the one who sincerely seeks truth for Allah's pleasure will be helped by Allah, while the one who follows his own desires and seeks fame will be deprived of beneficial knowledge. He cites Quranic warning against arrogance. The passage ends with a supplication for forgiveness.

Key Terms

مخطى آثم
مخلد في النار

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that all ijtihad is valid in all matters, and that any mujtahid is excused even in creed.
Correction: The passage clarifies that in doctrinal matters, only one view is correct, and the one who opposes the truth is sinful and eternally punished, with no excuse of ignorance or ijtihad.

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the ruling on a mujtahid who errs in a doctrinal matter (عقلية)?
A) He is rewarded like a correct mujtahid.
B) He is not excused and is eternally in the Fire.
C) He is excused if he is ignorant.
D) He is sinful but not eternally punished.

Key Takeaway
Doctrinal matters are unique; only one position is correct, and opposing it is a sin with eternal consequences, regardless of ijtihad or ignorance.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In your pursuit of Islamic knowledge, how much of your effort is driven by sincere search for Allah's pleasure, and how much by the desire for recognition, followers, or status? The author warns that the arrogant seeker is deprived of light. What will you change starting today to ensure your intentions are pure?
?
You have just learned that ignorance is no excuse in doctrinal matters. Is there any core belief you hold that you have not thoroughly verified, assuming Allah would forgive your ignorance? What concrete steps will you take this week to resolve any uncertainty in your faith?
?
Consider the sincere seeker whom Allah helps and through whom He guides others. Are you such a person? Or have you been content with superficial knowledge and following others without conviction? What is one area of your faith where you need to move from blind imitation to certain belief, and how will you begin that journey?
